The ProblemÂ \u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ERight now, instead of working to improve the economy, address the housing crisis, or focus on the many pressing issues facing Americans, our government is arguing over how to ignore the will of voters in 2026 and beyond â an election still a year away.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIâm talking about partisan redistricting, also known as gerrymandering, which has led to some of the most ruthless, self-serving, and undemocratic politics in our countryâs history.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThis petition offers a national solution to end gerrymandering once and for all \u003Cem\u003Ebefore the problem gets even worse.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn Texas and Missouri, Republican lawmakers are close to redrawing district lines five years early, rather than waiting until 2030 like the rest of the country. Our Plan to End Gerrymandering\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E1) Ban Mid-Decade Redistricting:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EStates are supposed to redraw maps once every ten years after the Census â and for good reason. Allowing redistricting at any time destroys stability and fairness in congressional representation. Congress must mandate that all states redraw maps only once per decade.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EÂ \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E2) Require States to Prevent Gerrymandering by Adopting One of Two Redistricting Systems:\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EÂ  Â  Â a) Independent Commissions:Â \u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThirteen states already use independent commissions, which empower a group of cross-partisan voters to determine districts. \u003Cem\u003EI have direct experience implementing this kind of reform:Â \u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn 2016, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=oIAQcvewgTg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003EI led the successful effort to establish Michiganâs independent commission\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which remains in place today. The result? The people of Michigan now have far more competitive districts and a much more responsive state government.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIndependent commissions are a straightforward and relatively easy-to-implement solution that mitigates some of the worst aspects of gerrymandering.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHowever, these commissions can still leave voters unrepresented. For example, in California, the percentage of Republican voters in the state is higher than the percentage of GOP house seats. This seemingly inescapable disparity is why many reformers prefer the following option...\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EÂ \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EÂ  Â  Â b) Proportional Representation:Â \u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESeveral developed democracies use proportional representation in large part because it makes partisan redistricting nearly impossible.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EInstead of electing one representative per district, voters elect multiple representatives from larger, multi-member districts. Seats are awarded based on the percentage of the vote each party receives.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor example, New York currently has 26 single-member congressional districts. Under proportional representation, the state could be divided into five large districts, each electing five or six representatives. If a district votes 60% Democrat and 40% Republican, it would send 3 Democrats and 2 Republicans to Congress.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis system eliminates the winner-take-all structure that allows gerrymandering to thrive and gives voters of all backgrounds meaningful representation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYou can learn more about proportional representation \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ffairvote.org\u002Four-reforms\u002Fproportional-representation\u002F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003Ehere\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.Â \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EBoth options have benefits and drawbacks. Independent commissions are simple, but do not put an end to gerrymandering. While proportional representation systems have proven to be more effective, but require more radical change that people may not be prepared for. The point is, either option is better than the systems that Texas, Illinois, and Missouri, and other states have.Â \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAs someone whoâs worked closely on this issue, I know Republican, Democratic, and independent voters are all tired of hearing about gerrymandering.
